Task instruction sent to agent 
# Fix Windows Log Output Line Ending Normalization

**Repository:** navidrome/navidrome
**Language:** Go
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

Navidrome does not format log output correctly for Windows users. Logs use only line feed characters (`\n`), which makes them hard to read in standard Windows text editors. When existing carriage return + line feed sequences (`\r\n`) are present, they may not be preserved correctly. Logs written in multiple partial steps can also produce inconsistent line endings.

## Reproduction

1. Start Navidrome on Windows and generate some log output
2. Open the log file in Notepad and check the line endings
3. Write logs that include only line feeds, as well as logs with existing carriage returns and line feeds
4. Observe that the formatting is incorrect or inconsistent

## Key Components

- Log output/formatting code — where log lines are written to output
- Platform-specific line ending handling (Windows vs. Unix)

## Task

1. Locate the log output formatting code in Navidrome
2. On Windows, convert `\n` line endings to `\r\n` in log output
3. Preserve existing `\r\n` sequences without double-conversion (don't produce `\r\r\n`)
4. Ensure correct behavior when logs are written in multiple partial steps
5. Run existing tests to ensure no regressions

## Success Criteria

- Log output on Windows uses `\r\n` line endings
- Existing `\r\n` sequences are preserved unchanged
- Partial/multi-step log writes produce consistent line endings
- Unix behavior is unchanged
- All existing tests pass

     1→package log
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"strings"
     5→	"time"
     6→)
     7→
     8→func ShortDur(d time.Duration) string {
     9→	var s string
    10→	switch {
    11→	case d > time.Hour:
    12→		s = d.Round(time.Minute).String()
    13→	case d > time.Minute:
    14→		s = d.Round(time.Second).String()
    15→	case d > time.Second:
    16→		s = d.Round(10 * time.Millisecond).String()
    17→	case d > time.Millisecond:
    18→		s = d.Round(100 * time.Microsecond).String()
    19→	default:
    20→		s = d.String()
    21→	}
    22→	s = strings.TrimSuffix(s, "0s")
    23→	return strings.TrimSuffix(s, "0m")
    24→}
    25→

     1→package log
     2→
     3→// Copied from https://github.com/whuang8/redactrus (MIT License)
     4→// Copyright (c) 2018 William Huang
     5→
     6→import (
     7→	"fmt"
     8→	"reflect"
     9→	"regexp"
    10→
    11→	"github.com/sirupsen/logrus"
    12→)
    13→
    14→// Hook is a logrus hook for redacting information from logs
    15→type Hook struct {
    16→	// Messages with a log level not contained in this array
    17→	// will not be dispatched. If empty, all messages will be dispatched.
    18→	AcceptedLevels []logrus.Level
    19→	RedactionList  []string
    20→	redactionKeys  []*regexp.Regexp
    21→}
    22→
    23→// Levels returns the user defined AcceptedLevels
    24→// If AcceptedLevels is empty, all logrus levels are returned
    25→func (h *Hook) Levels() []logrus.Level {
    26→	if len(h.AcceptedLevels) == 0 {
    27→		return logrus.AllLevels
    28→	}
    29→	return h.AcceptedLevels
    30→}
    31→
    32→// Fire redacts values in a log Entry that match
    33→// with keys defined in the RedactionList
    34→func (h *Hook) Fire(e *logrus.Entry) error {
    35→	if err := h.initRedaction(); err != nil {
    36→		return err
    37→	}
    38→	for _, re := range h.redactionKeys {
    39→		// Redact based on key matching in Data fields
    40→		for k, v := range e.Data {
    41→			if re.MatchString(k) {
    42→				e.Data[k] = "[REDACTED]"
    43→				continue
    44→			}
    45→
    46→			// Redact based on value matching in Data fields
    47→			switch reflect.TypeOf(v).Kind() {
    48→			case reflect.String:
    49→				e.Data[k] = re.ReplaceAllString(v.(string), "$1[REDACTED]$2")
    50→				continue
    51→			case reflect.Map:
    52→				s := fmt.Sprintf("%+v", v)
    53→				e.Data[k] = re.ReplaceAllString(s, "$1[REDACTED]$2")
    54→				c
... (truncated)

     1→package log
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"io"
     5→	"runtime"
     6→)
     7→
     8→// CRLFWriter wraps an io.Writer and converts LF line endings to CRLF on Windows.
     9→// It preserves existing CRLF sequences without double-conversion.
    10→type CRLFWriter struct {
    11→	w           io.Writer
    12→	lastWasCR   bool // Track if the last byte written was '\r'
    13→	convertCRLF bool // Only convert on Windows
    14→}
    15→
    16→// NewCRLFWriter creates a new CRLF writer that wraps the given io.Writer.
    17→// On Windows, it converts LF ('\n') to CRLF ('\r\n').
    18→// On other platforms, it passes through unchanged.
    19→func NewCRLFWriter(w io.Writer) *CRLFWriter {
    20→	return &CRLFWriter{
    21→		w:           w,
    22→		lastWasCR:   false,
    23→		convertCRLF: runtime.GOOS == "windows",
    24→	}
    25→}
    26→
    27→// Write implements io.Writer. It converts line endings from LF to CRLF on Windows.
    28→func (cw *CRLFWriter) Write(p []byte) (n int, err error) {
    29→	if !cw.convertCRLF {
    30→		// On non-Windows platforms, write directly without conversion
    31→		return cw.w.Write(p)
    32→	}
    33→
    34→	// On Windows, convert LF to CRLF, but avoid double-conversion for existing CRLF
    35→	var buf []byte
    36→	for i := 0; i < len(p); i++ {
    37→		b := p[i]
    38→		if b == '\n' && !cw.lastWasCR {
    39→			// This is a LF not preceded by CR, so add CR before it
    40→			buf = append(buf, '\r', '\n')
    41→		} else {
    42→			buf = append(buf, b)
    43→		}
    44→		cw.lastWasCR = (b == '\r')
    45→	}
    46→
    47→	// Write the converted buffer
    48→	_, err = cw.w.Write(buf)
    49→	// Return the number of bytes from the original input that were processed
    50→	return len(p), err
    51→}
    52→

... (truncated)

131-assistanttext-
Perfect! All tests pass. Let me create a summary of the implementation:

## Summary

I've successfully implemented Windows log output line ending normalization in Navidrome. Here's what was done:

### Implementation Overview

**1. Created a new `CRLFWriter` wrapper** (`/app/log/lineendings.go`):
- Wraps any `io.Writer` to convert line endings
- On Windows: converts `\n` (LF) to `\r\n` (CRLF)
- On non-Windows: passes through unchanged
- **Key feature**: Tracks the last character written to preserve existing `\r\n` sequences without double-conversion
- Handles partial/multi-step writes correctly by maintaining `lastWasCR` state across writes

**2. Integrated the custom writer** (`/app/log/log.go`):
- Modified the logger initialization in the `init()` function
- Wrapped `os.Stderr` with `NewCRLFWriter()` 
- This ensures all log output is properly formatted before being written

**3. Added comprehensive tests** (`/app/log/log_test.go`):
- 11 new test cases covering all edge cases:
  - LF to CRLF conversion
  - Preserving existing CRLF sequences
  - Mixed LF and CRLF handling
  - Partial writes with CR at boundaries
  - Multiple consecutive LF characters
  - Empty writes and CR-only sequences
  - CR state tracking across multiple writes
  - Cross-platform behavior (pass-through on non-Windows)

### Key Features

✅ **Converts `\n` to `\r\n` on Windows**
- Logs written with LF-only line endings are automatically converted

✅ **Preserves existing `\r\n` sequences**
- Prevents double-conversion to `\r\r\n`
- Tracks state across writes to handle boundaries correctly

✅ **Handles partial/multi-step writes**
- Maintains state between write calls
- Correctly handles cases where CR is at the end of one write and LF at the start of the next

✅ **Unix behavior unchanged**
- On non-Wind

If empty, all messages will be dispatched.\n\tAcceptedLevels []logrus.Level\n\tRedactionList  []string\n\tredactionKeys  []*regexp.Regexp\n}\n\n// Levels returns the user defined AcceptedLevels\n// If AcceptedLevels is empty, all logrus levels are returned\nfunc (h *Hook) Levels() []logrus.Level {\n\tif len(h.AcceptedLevels) == 0 {\n\t\treturn logrus.AllLevels\n\t}\n\treturn h.AcceptedLevels\n}\n\n// Fire redacts values in a log Entry that match\n// with keys defined in the RedactionList\nfunc (h *Hook) Fire(e *logrus.Entry) error {\n\tif err := h.initRedaction(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tfor _, re := range h.redactionKeys {\n\t\t// Redact based on key matching in Data fields\n\t\tfor k, v := range e.Data {\n\t\t\tif re.MatchString(k) {\n\t\t\t\te.Data[k] = \"[REDACTED]\"\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Redact based on value matching in Data fields\n\t\t\tswitch reflect.TypeOf(v).Kind() {\n\t\t\tcase reflect.String:\n\t\t\t\te.Data[k] = re.ReplaceAllString(v.(string), \"$1[REDACTED]$2\")\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\tcase reflect.Map:\n\t\t\t\ts := fmt.Sprintf(\"%+v\", v)\n\t\t\t\te.Data[k] = re.ReplaceAllString(s, \"$1[REDACTED]$2\")\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Redact based on text matching in the Message field\n\t\te.Message = re.ReplaceAllString(e.Message, \"$1[REDACTED]$2\")\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (h *Hook) initRedaction() error {\n\tif len(h.redactionKeys) == 0 {\n\t\tfor _, redactionKey := range h.RedactionList {\n\t\t\tre, err := regexp.Compile(redactionKey)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\th.redactionKeys = append(h.redactionKeys, re)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (h *Hook) redact(msg string) (string, error) {\n\tif err := h.initRedaction(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn msg, err\n\t}\n\tfor _, re := range h.redactionKeys {\n\t\tmsg = re.ReplaceAllString(msg, \"$1[REDACTED]$2\")\n\t}\n\n\treturn msg, nil\n}\n",

It converts line endings from LF to CRLF on Windows.\nfunc (cw *CRLFWriter) Write(p []byte) (n int, err error) {\n\tif !cw.convertCRLF {\n\t\t// On non-Windows platforms, write directly without conversion\n\t\treturn cw.w.Write(p)\n\t}\n\n\t// On Windows, convert LF to CRLF, but avoid double-conversion for existing CRLF\n\tvar buf []byte\n\tfor i := 0; i < len(p); i++ {\n\t\tb := p[i]\n\t\tif b == '\\n' && !cw.lastWasCR {\n\t\t\t// This is a LF not preceded by CR, so add CR before it\n\t\t\tbuf = append(buf, '\\r', '\\n')\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tbuf = append(buf, b)\n\t\t}\n\t\tcw.lastWasCR = (b == '\\r')\n\t}\n\n\t// Write the converted buffer\n\t_, err = cw.w.Write(buf)\n\t// Return the number of bytes from the original input that were processed\n\treturn len(p), err\n}\n",

        "+  Describe(\"CRLFWriter\", func() {",
        "+    var buf *bytes.Buffer",
        "+    var writer *CRLFWriter",
        "+",
        "+    // crlfWriterForceWindows creates a CRLFWriter with Windows mode forced on for testing",
        "+    crlfWriterForceWindows := func(w io.Writer) *CRLFWriter {",
        "+      return &CRLFWriter{",
        "+        w:           w,",
        "+        lastWasCR:   false,",
        "+        convertCRLF: true,",
        "+      }",
        "+    }",
        "+",
        "+    BeforeEach(func() {",
        "+      buf = &bytes.Buffer{}",
        "+      writer = NewCRLFWriter(buf)",
        "+    })",
        "+",
        "+    Context(\"on non-Windows platforms\", func() {",
        "+      It(\"passes through data unchanged\", func() {",
        "+        if runtime.GOOS == \"windows\" {",
        "+          Skip(\"This test is for non-Windows platforms only\")",
        "+        }",
        "+",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\nline2\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(12))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\nline2\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+    })",
        "+",
        "+    Context(\"on Windows (forced)\", func() {",
        "+      BeforeEach(func() {",
        "+        buf = &bytes.Buffer{}",
        "+        writer = crlfWriterForceWindows(buf)",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"converts LF to CRLF\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\nline2\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(12))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\nline2\\r\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"preserves existing CRLF without double-conversion\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\r\\nline2\\r\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(14))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\nline2\\r\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles mixed LF and CRLF\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\nline2\\r\\nline3\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(19))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\nline2\\r\\nline3\\r\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles partial writes correctly\", func() {",
        "+        // First write: partial line with CR at the end",
        "+        n1, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\r\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n1).To(Equal(6))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\"))",
        "+",
        "+        // Second write: LF following the CR from previous write",
        "+        n2, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"\\nline2\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n2).To(Equal(7))",
        "+        // The second write should recognize that the previous write ended with CR",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\nline2\\r\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles multiple consecutive LF characters\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\n\\nline2\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(12))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\n\\r\\nline2\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles string with only LF\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"\\n\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(1))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"\\r\\n\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles empty write\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(0))",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"handles CR without LF\", func() {",
        "+        n, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\rline2\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n).To(Equal(11))",
        "+        // CR without LF should pass through unchanged",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\rline2\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+",
        "+      It(\"tracks CR state across multiple writes\", func() {",
        "+        // First write ends with CR",
        "+        n1, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"line1\\r\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n1).To(Equal(6))",
        "+",
        "+        // Second write starts with LF (should not add another CR)",
        "+        n2, err := writer.Write([]byte(\"\\nline2\"))",
        "+        Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())",
        "+        Expect(n2).To(Equal(6))",
        "+",
        "+        // Result should be \"line1\\r\\nline2\", not \"line1\\r\\r\\nline2\"",
        "+        Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal(\"line1\\r\\nline2\"))",
        "+      })",
        "+    })",
        "+  })",
        " })"
      ],
      "newLines": 123,
      "newStart": 249,
      "oldLines": 4,
      "oldStart": 249
    }
  ],
  "userModified": false

It converts line endings from LF to CRLF on Windows.\nfunc (cw *CRLFWriter) Write(p []byte) (n int, err error) {\n\tif !cw.convertCRLF {\n\t\t// On non-Windows platforms, write directly without conversion\n\t\treturn cw.w.Write(p)\n\t}\n\n\t// On Windows, convert LF to CRLF, but avoid double-conversion for existing CRLF\n\tvar buf []byte\n\tfor i := 0; i < len(p); i++ {\n\t\tb := p[i]\n\t\tif b == '\\n' && !cw.lastWasCR {\n\t\t\t// This is a LF not preceded by CR, so add CR before it\n\t\t\tbuf = append(buf, '\\r', '\\n')\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tbuf = append(buf, b)\n\t\t}\n\t\tcw.lastWasCR = (b == '\\r')\n\t}\n\n\t// Write the converted buffer\n\t_, err = cw.w.Write(buf)\n\t// Return the number of bytes from the original input that were processed\n\treturn len(p), err\n}\n",

1. WRITE /app/log/lineendings.go
package log

import (
	"io"
	"runtime"
)

// CRLFWriter wraps an io.Writer and converts LF line endings to CRLF on Windows.
// It preserves existing CRLF sequences without double-conversion.
type CRLFWriter struct {
	w           io.Writer
	lastWasCR   bool // Track if the last byte written was '\r'
	convertCRLF bool // Only convert on Windows
}

// NewCRLFWriter creates a new CRLF writer that wraps the given io.Writer.
// On Windows, it converts LF ('\n') to CRLF ('\r\n').
// On other platforms, it passes through unchanged.
func NewCRLFWriter(w io.Writer) *CRLFWriter {
	return &CRLFWriter{
		w:           w,
		lastWasCR:   false,
		convertCRLF: runtime.GOOS == "windows",
	}
}

// Write implements io.Writer. It converts line endings from LF to CRLF on Windows.
func (cw *CRLFWriter) Write(p []byte) (n int, err error) {
	if !cw.convertCRLF {
		// On non-Windows platforms, write directly without conversion
		return cw.w.Write(p)
	}

	// On Windows, convert LF to CRLF, but avoid double-conversion for existing CRLF
	var buf []byte
	for i := 0; i < len(p); i++ {
		b := p[i]
		if b == '\n' && !cw.lastWasCR {
			// This is a LF not preceded by CR, so add CR before it
			buf = append(buf, '\r', '\n')
		} else {
			buf = append(buf, b)
		}
		cw.lastWasCR = (b == '\r')
	}

	// Write the converted buffer
	_, err = cw.w.Write(buf)
	// Return the number of bytes from the original input that were processed
	return len(p), err
}

package log

import (
	"bytes"
	"runtime"
	"testing"

	. "github.com/onsi/ginkgo/v2"
	. "github.com/onsi/gomega"
)

func TestLineEndings(t *testing.T) {
	RegisterFailHandler(Fail)
	RunSpecs(t, "Line Endings Suite")
}

var _ = Describe("CRLFWriter", func() {
	var buf *bytes.Buffer
	var writer *CRLFWriter

	BeforeEach(func() {
		buf = &bytes.Buffer{}
		writer = NewCRLFWriter(buf)
	})

	Context("on non-Windows platforms", func() {
		It("passes through data unchanged", func() {
			if runtime.GOOS == "windows" {
				Skip("This test is for non-Windows platforms only")
			}

			n, err := writer.Write([]byte("line1\nline2\n"))
			Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())
			Expect(n).To(Equal(12))
			Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal("line1\nline2\n"))
		})
	})

	Context("on Windows", func() {
		SkipIfNot := func(g bool, reason string) {
			if !g && runtime.GOOS != "windows" {
				Skip(reason)
			}
		}

		It("converts LF to CRLF", func() {
			SkipIfNot(runtime.GOOS == "windows", "This test is for Windows only")

			n, err := writer.Write([]byte("line1\nline2\n"))
			Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())
			Expect(n).To(Equal(12))
			Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal("line1\r\nline2\r\n"))
		})

		It("preserves existing CRLF without double-conversion", func() {
			SkipIfNot(runtime.GOOS == "windows", "This test is for Windows only")

			n, err := writer.Write([]byte("line1\r\nline2\r\n"))
			Expect(err).NotTo(HaveOccurred())
			Expect(n).To(Equal(14))
			Expect(buf.String()).To(Equal("line1\r\nline2\r\n"))
		})

			SkipIfNot(runtime.GOOS == "windows", "This test is for Windows only")

			n, err := writer.Write([]byte("line1\nline2\r\nline3\n"))

	defaultLogger.Level = logrus.TraceLevel
	_, file, _, ok := runtime.Caller(0)
	if !ok {
		return
	}
	rootPath = strings.TrimSuffix(file, "log/log.go")

func init() {
	defaultLogger.Level = logrus.TraceLevel
	// On Windows, wrap stderr with a CRLF converter to normalize line endings
	defaultLogger.SetOutput(NewCRLFWriter(os.Stderr))
	_, file, _, ok := runtime.Caller(0)
	if !ok {
		return
	}
	rootPath = strings.TrimSuffix(file, "log/log.go")
}

			Expect(hook.LastEntry().Message).To(Equal("A crash happened"))
